ARIE 1917-1918 [vol. 040]


A.--List of copper-plates examined during the year 1917-18.


ARIE/1917-1918/A/1917-18/1 (page 11)
Placement
The Superintendent, Govern-ment Museum, Madras.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
Śā??āhana-Śaka 431, Sarvadhārin, Piṟaṭṭāśi 13.
Language
Tamil
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
…
Remarks
The date is wrong. But Kali 4031 curiously enough corresponds to the cyclic year Sarva-dhārin. This is evidently another forgery of the type of No. 1 of Appendix A to the Annual Report for 1909 and No. 6 of Appen-dix A to the Annual Report for 1910. See above part 1, paragraph 15.
ARIE/1917-1918/A/1917-18/2 (page 11)
Placement
The Reddy of Sivaram, through the Tahsildar of Madakasira, Anantapur district.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
Śaka 1665, Rudhirōd-gārin. Śrā-vaṇa, śu. di. prathamā, Monday.
Language
Kanarese
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
…
Remarks
Refers to the foundation of a village called Chandraśēkharapura by Medakeri-Nāyaka son of Mahānayaka Kāmagēti Kastūri Bara-maṇṇa-Nāyaka, on which occasion the right of worship in the temple of Hanumanta at Chitrapuri was claimed by a certain Raṅgā-chārya, the priest of the Pomboḷala-Gopālas-vāmin temple, which the Nāyaka granted.
ARIE/1917-1918/A/1917-18/3 (page 11)

…
Remarks
Similar to No. 12 of Appendix A to the Annual Report for 1906. The inscription is evi-dently a forgery. The name of the village granted is not clear, three to four lines at this place being written on erasure. See below Part II, paragraph 7.
ARIE/1917-1918/A/1917-18/4 (page 11)
Placement
M.R.Ry. M. Kalidasu Garu, High Court Vakil, Guntur.
Dynasty
Telugu-Chōḍa.
King
Śaṁbhu-Chōḍadēva of the Kuśa family, residing at Nelluhāpura.
Date
50th year
Language
Sanskrit, (Nāgarī)
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
…
Remarks
Incomplete. Registers the gift of the village Kummaḍūru on the bank of the Tuṅga-bhadra by the king on the occasion of the installation of his two sons Agastīśvara-Chōḍa and Shaṇmukha-Chōḍa as yuvarājas. The village was divided into four shares two of which were given to the gods A gastyēśvara at Mandhara and Kumarasvāmin at Tām-rapura. The third was given to his own purōhit and the fourth to the worshippers, servants, etc., of the two temples.
ARIE/1917-1918/A/1917-18/5 (page 11)
Placement
Do.
Dynasty
Vijayanaga-ra.
King
Sadāśiva-Mahārāya
Date
Śaka 1478, Naḷa, Śrā-vaṇa, ba. di. ashṭamī, jayanti. Thursday.
Language
Sanskrit, (Nāgarī)
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
…
Remarks
These are the missing third and fourth plates of No. 24 of Appendix A, to the Annual Report for 1917 with which the grant is complete. Registers the grant, with all the incomes, of the village Marripūṇḍi surnamed Raghu-nāthapuram situated in the Valanāḍu division of the Koṇḍavīḍu-sīma to the great scholar and astronomer Sarvā-Bhaṭṭa, who belonged to the Yāska-gōtra and Āpastamba-sūtra and was a Yajurvēdin. He was the son of Koṇḍu-Bhaṭṭa and grandson of Sarvā-Bhaṭṭa and was a resident of the village Penumpnali as also a devotee of the god Gōkaraṇadēva. The gift was made on the representation of the king's minister Rāma-rāja.

Remarks
Registers the tax-free gift of the village Arātaha in the Vāsudēvakhaṇḍa-vishaya by the king to some Brāhmaṇas some of whom were of the Vājasanēya-charaṇa and Kaṇva-śākhā while the others were of the Vatsa-gōtra. The king was the son of Raṇabhaṇja-dēva, the grandson of Śatrubhaṇjadēva and the great-grandson of Śilābhaṇjadēva.

Remarks
States that the king granted, tax-free, the village Mula-Māchhāḍa in the Māchhāḍa-khaṇḍa-vishaya to a Brahman named Bha-[ṭṭa]-Purandara, son of Dēvaḍaśarman and grandson of Hariśaśarman of the Vājasanēya-charaṇa and the Rauhita-gōtra. The king was the son of Śilābhaṇjadēva, grandson of Digbhaṇjadēva and the great-grandson of Raṇabhaṇjadēva.

Records the tax-free gift of the village Mach-chhaḍa in the Machhākhaṇḍa-vishaya by the king to Bha[ṭṭa] Rudaḍa, the son of Kēśava and the grandson of Charamvasvāmin of the Vājasanēya-charaṇa and of the Vatsa-gōtra. The king's ancestry is the same as in No. 6 above.

…
Remarks
Registers the grant of some land in the village Amēraśiṅga of the Jalamvōra-vishaya by the king to Svāmiśarman, son of Bhaṭṭaputra, of the Vājaśana (i.e., Vājasanēya) charaṇa, Kanma (i.e., Kaṇva)-śākhā and Jātukarṇa-gōtra. The king is said to have been the lord of Kaliṅga; and Śvētakādhisṭhāna is mentioned.
ARIE/1917-1918/A/1917-18/10 (page 12)
Placement
Do.
Dynasty
Bhañja
King
Yaśabhaṁjadēva, ruling over the [Khi]ṇjalidēśa.
Date
[3]rd year Kārttika, śu. di. ēkādaśī.
Language
Sanskrit, (Nāgarī)
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
…
Remarks
Records the grant of the village Komyāṇa in the Vōḍā-vishaya with all its income to the Dīkshita Jagadharaśarman, of the village Paḍhuvāḍapāḍhaka in the Koṇṭaravēṅga-vishaya. The donee belonged to the Bhārad-vāja-gōtra and Mādhvandinīya-śākhā and was a student of the Yajur-vēda. He was well-versed in the Śrauta and Smārta rituals and was strong in astronomy (j[y]ōtiś-śāśtra). The grant was made on the uchchayana-ēkādaśī day in the bright half of the Kārtika month when Vishṇu is believed to wake up from his four-months' sleep.
ARIE/1917-1918/A/1917-18/11 (page 13)

M.R.Ry. V.Rangacharya Avargal, M.A., Presidency College, Madras.

Edition
…
Remarks
States that the king granted the village Kombaṟu lying one gavyūta to the south of the village Vleṇṭūru in the Kanthēṟ[u]vāṭi-vishaya, to a scholar in the Vēdas and the Śāśtras named Sōmaśarman, who was the son of Svāmiśarman and grandson of Dēvaśar-man. The last was a Taittirīya Brahma-chārin of the Gārgya-gōtra and a master of the four Śāśtras.

Remarks
Registers the gift of the village Madhipathara-khaṇḍa [in] the Mahēndra-bhōga to a certain Ujaṇaka by Rāṇaka Śrī-Dharmakhēdi, son of Mahāmaṇḍalēśvara Rāṇaka Śrī-Bhāmakhēdi of the Kadamva (i.e., Kadamba) family, the lord of five vishayas (pañchavishayādhipati). The order of gift is addressed to the officials and people of the Paṁchapātra-vishaya.

Remarks
The plates are so very faintly engraved in characters of about the 9th century that it is almost impossible to read them. Register the grant of the village Tāmvaddi in [Śaila ..]-vishaya. The donee's name is not clear. The grant was issued from Kaliṅganagara.

Remarks
Records the gift of a land growing 1,000 are-ca-nut trees, another land sowable with 50 khaṇḍikas of paddy-seed and a house-site in the village Attili in the Attili-vishaya, to the songstress Challavā who was the daughter of Mallapa, the son of Thuṇḍakā who was no less than an apsaras in beauty.

Remarks
Registers the grant by the king of the village Rāvulapaṟti, surnaming it Unḍīśapuram, to a number of Brahmans as an agrahāra. It also records the names of a dozen other villages similarly granted by him to Brah-mans the king's capital is mentioned to be Sūravaram.
ARIE/1917-1918/A/1917-18/17 (page 13)

Remarks
This is a sale-deed executed by three indivi-duals of the village Pōtulapuri to two other individuals waiving permanently the right of collecting certain taxes payable to them, for the consideration of 50 ghaṭi-varahālu received as the commutation amount.
ARIE/1917-1918/A/1917-18/18 (page 14)
Placement
M.R.Ry. Rama Rao, Contrac-tor, Lepakshi (same taluk and district).
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
Śaka 1602 Durmati, Vaiśākha, su. di. tṛitīyā.
Language
Telugu
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
…
Remarks
States that, while Liṅgōji-Paṇḍita was govern-ing the Karnāṭaka kingdom from Penu-goṇḍa-paṭṭaṇa as a subordinate of Akhanna-Paṇḍita, the younger brother of Mādanna-Paṇḍita who was the best of Brahmans and the chief officer of the king of Bhāgnagar, Nañjappa of the Kāmakāyana-Viśvāmitra-gōtra, Āśvalāyana-sūtra and Ṛik-sākhā who was the sthaḷa-karṇam of Lēpākshi in the Roddhanāṭi-sthaḷa in Penugoṇḍa-rājya gave some land in that village to Kumārayya of the Bhāradvāja-gōtra, Āpastamba-sūtra and Yajuś-śākhā, who was the ārādhya at Lēpākshi. It registers also the gift of rates on pack-bullocks, shops, looms and marriages to the same Kumārayya by the samayins of Ayyāvaḷi, etc., the Vaiśyas of the 102 gōtras, the representatives of maṭhas the Yajamānas of the Lēpākshi-sthala, etc., assembled in the temple maṇḍapa of that place for daily offerings and lamps to the god Nañjuṇḍēśvara.
ARIE/1917-1918/A/1917-18/19 (page 14)

The Village Munsiff of Soma-ghatta, (Hindupur taluk, Anantapur district).

Language
Telugu
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
…
Remarks
States that a certain Pedda Ahōbalareḍḍi who was a divān under Mahāmaṇḍalēśvara Kṛishṇadēvarāya who was ruliṅg at Penu-goṇḍa built a temple to Ahōbala Madhugiri-Lakshmī Nṛisiṁhasvāmin at Sōmaghaṭṭa in accordance with the direction given to him by the deity at Ahōbalam in a dream. Registers the gift of the village Kinirāḷḷa-palle in the Gōraṇṭla-samutu by the king for offerings and some gold for lamps to the god and of certain contributions by the karṇam of Sōmaghaṭṭa.
ARIE/1917-1918/A/1917-18/20 (page 14)
Placement
The Shrotriyamdar of Yajna-settipalli (Hindupur taluk, Anantapur district).
Dynasty
Vijaya-nagara.
King
…
Date
…
Language
Sanskṛit in Nāgarī
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
…
Remarks
The record is incomplete, only the first 3 plates of the set remaining. It stops with the partial description of the qualities of king Śrīraṅga, the son of Pedda Veṅkaṭapati who was the second son of Śrīraṅga, the son of the great Rāmarāja who was the minister of Śadāśiva. See the genealogical table, Epi-graphia Indica Vol. III, page 238. The king is stated to have been crowned by Tātayārya.
ARIE/1917-1918/A/1917-18/21 (page 15)
Placement
The Tahsildar of Madakasira (same taluk and district).
Dynasty
…
King
Mahārāja Bukkarāya
Date
Śaka 1305, Prabhava, Phālguṇa.
Language
Kanarese & Nāgarī
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
…
Remarks
The Śaka date falls into the reign of Virūpāk-sha I predecessor of Bukka II. Registers in detail the incomes that the guarding officers (kāvulu-doregalu) of Maḍakaśīrya were to get from the several classes of people, residing in the village. Also specifies the incomes that the āyagāras (i.e., the village servants) of certain villages were to get since the tank at Harive was repaired.
ARIE/1917-1918/A/1917-18/22 (page 15)
Placement
The District Judge, Madura
Dynasty
…
King
Rāya Vijaya-Raghunātha Toṇḍaimāṉār, ruling over the Madurai-nāḍu.
Date
Śaka 1687, Kali 4866, Pārthiva, Tai, 4, Friday, śu. di. pañchamī, Uttara (Uttara-Phalgunī), Amṛitayōga, Bālavā-ka-raṇa.
Language
Tamil
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
…
Remarks
Registers the grant of land at Kāraippaṭṭi, hamlet of Paḻanivaḍam made by the king for certain services and charities to be con-ducted at the time of the festivals of the god Bāla-Subrahmaṇya on the Paḻaṇi-hill on the bank of the Shaṇmukhanadī in the Vaigāvūr-nāḍu. The grant was executed in favour of Subrahmaṇya-Uḍaiyar, son of Pulittōlu Mallikārjuna-Uḍaiyar, residing at the Paḻaṇi-kshētra. A certain Ḍabīr Veṅkaṭarāyar was given land and entrusted with the charity. The coin Rājagōpali is mentioned.

B.--Stone inscriptions copied in 1917 (continued from last Annual Report).

Remarks
Records a sale of land as a tax-free dēvadāna by the resi-dents of Iḷanagar, a village in Ādaṉūr-nāḍu a subdivision of Kē[ra*]ḷāntaka-vaḷanāḍu to the temple of Madurāntaka-Īśvaramuḍaiyār at Nagaram Madurāntakapuram in the same nāḍu. The vendors agreed to pay the taxes on the land.

Remarks
Incomplete. Records that, in accordance with the order of Naḍuvirukkum Paśalai Kṛishṇa Bhaṭṭar who settled the district (nāḍū kūru śeygira), the merchants (nagarattōm) of Madurāntakapuram in Taṭṭaigaḷa-nāḍu, which was a subdivision of Kēraḷa-nāḍu, apportioned the tax-free dēvadāna lands of the temple of Madurānta-Īśvara-muḍaiyār which were situated in Kshatriśikhāmaṇi-chaturvēdimaṅgalam, Śāttaṉūr, and Iḷanagar in Ādaṉūr-nāḍu, for offerings, lamps, śrībali and other services in the shrines of Śrīkaraṇaviṭaṅka and Umāparamēśvarī.
ARIE/1917-1918/B/1917/194 (page 16)
Placement
On the same wall
Dynasty
Chōḷa
King
Parakēsarivarman [alias] Uḍaiyār śrī-Rājēndra-Chōḷadēva I.
Date
15+22nd (kīḻ) year.
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Incomplete. Records a sale of land to the temple of Madu-rāntaka-Īśvarattu-Mahādēva at Madurāntakapuram by the great assembly of Kshatriyaśikhāmaṇi-chaturvēdimaṅ-galam, a brahmadēya in Taṭṭaigaḷa-nāḍu, a subdivision of Kēraḷāntaka-vaḷanāḍu. The fragment below it seems to register a gift of land to a private individual who was found on examination fit by the officer (adhikārin) Iru-maḍiśōḻa-Mūvēndavēḷār to have performed the consecra-tion ceremony of the god Madurāntaka Īśvaramuḍaiyār properly.

ARIE/1917-1918/B/1917/197 (page 17)
Placement
On the north and west walls of the Añjalākshi Ammaṉ shrine in the same temple.
Dynasty
Koṅgu-Pāṇḍya.
King
Rājakēsarivarman alias Tribhuvana-chakravartin Vīra-Pāṇḍyadēva.
Date
15th year
Language
Tamil

ARIE/1917-1918/B/1917/244 (page 21)
Placement
Do.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Tribhuvanachakravartin Rājarājadēva
Date
21st year and 80th day.
Language
Tamil
Remarks
In accordance with the order of the king, issued on the 20th year and 348th day of his reign, that the lands held by persons who proved treacherous should be sold in public auction (Rājarāja-peruvilai) for prices to be fixed by certain revenue officers, and that the sale-deeds should he given to purchasers signed by the officers of the taxation depart-ment, the holdings of two individuals at Guṇagaṇāntaḷi-maṅgalam in Paṉaiyūr-nāḍu were forfeited. Mentions the temple of Guṇatāṅgīśvaramuḍaiyār.

Language
Tamil
Remarks
Records that on the order of the king, the assembly of Rājarā-ja-chaturvēdimaṅgalam which was a free village in Jayaṅ-goṇḍa-Chōḷamaṇḍalam met together in the hall called Mummaḍiśōḻaṉ-maṇḍapa along with Nambi-Uḍuttūr-uḍaiyār who governed the village, and made a settle-ment (vyavasthai) regarding the incomes derived from lands belonging to a number of shrines and set apart for various services. Among the temples and deities men-tioned are Rājarāja-Viṇṇagar-Āḻvār, Kundavai-Viṇṇa-gar-Āḻvār, Sundaraśōḻa-Viṇṇagar-Āḻvār, Dēvēndra, Sarasvati, Śrī-Bhashṭārakiyār, Mahāmōḍiyār, Sūrya-dēva, Saptamātṛis, Mahāśāstā, Durgaiyār, Subrahmaṇya, Jyēshṭaiyār and the village gods.

Jaṭilavarman alias Tribhuvanachakra-vartin Kōnērmaikoṇḍāṉ Tirunelvēlip-perumāḷ Vīraveṇbāmālai alias Kula-śēkharadēva, son of Perumāḷ Abhirāma arākrama-Pāṇḍyadēva.
Date
Śaka 1477, 5th year, Rākshasa. Utta-ṛāyaṇa, Vasanta-ṛitu, Mēsha 9, śu. di. chaturdaśī, Gaja-karaṇa, [Har]shaṇa-yōga, Hasta.
Language
Grantha & Tamil
Remarks
The introduction commences with the words Bhuvanaika-vīra, etc. Records that prince Aḻagaṉ Perumāḷ Guṇa-rāma, born in the asterism Mūla, gave lands including Ariñjārpirāṭṭi in Kuṟumaṟai-nāḍu to the temple of Viśvanātha for a festival to be conducted on his birth-day every year. Refers to a dēvadāna belonging to a Muhammadan mosque (tulukkaṉ-paḷḷi).

Kanarese
Remarks
Much damaged. Registers the gift of the village of Do[ḍ]ḍēri surnamed Veṅkaṭēśvarasamudra in Agaḷi-sīme by the Mahānāyaṅkachārya Paṅgapa-Nayaka, son of Harati Lakshmīpati-Nāyaka of the Kāsyapa-gōtra. ARIE/1917-1918/B/1917/752 (page 78)
Placement
On another pillar in the same place.
Dynasty
Chōḷa
King
Uḍaiyār Śrī-Rājēndra-Chōḷadēva
Date
10th year
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Registers that the maṇḍapa (in which these pillars originally were) was commenced on the 160th day of this year and finished in 40 days by the general Araiyaṉ Rājaṛājaṉ alias Vikramaśōḻa-Śōḻiyavaraiyaṉ of Śāttamaṅgalam in Tiraimūr-nāḍu. Below the inscription are engraved the titles Edirttavarkālaṉ and Sāmantakēsari; see ibid and No. 24.

Anantapur district, Hindupur taluk.

ARIE/1917-1918/B/1917/766 (page 79)
Placement
On a boulder in a field below the tank bund in the same village.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
…
Language
Kanarese
Remarks
Bears the sentence ‘Svasti śrī Mandachariya bhasaṁ śandu-du’: “Hail ! the speech of the blessed Mandachari has proved true.” On another part of the stone are three lines of writing not quite legible. The first line seems to contain the name Chārurasibhaṇḍirar for Chārurāsi-Paṇ-ḍita, the title of a particular order of Jaina monks (see Ep. Carn., Vol. II, p. 61).

Śaka 1246, Rudhi-rōdgāri, Chaitra, śu. di. daśamī, Monday.
Language
Kanarese
Remarks
Refers to the victory gained by the Mahāpradhāna Āḷiya Mācheya-Daṇṇāyaka over a certain Rāchaya-Nāyaka of Tumbeyakallu. Also records the death of a hero evident-ly on the same occasion.
ARIE/1917-1918/B/1917/772 (page 80)
Placement
On two pieces of a broken hero-stone lying in the same place.
Dynasty
Hoysaḷa
King
Vīra-Baḷḷāḷadēva
Date
Śaka 1243, Raudri, Bhādrapada, ba. di. 13, Monday.
Language
Kanarese
Remarks
Records the death of the Mahāsāvantādhipati Hiriya Bommeya-Nāyaka, son of Gaṅgeya-Nāyka of Hoḷakallu, in a fight against the cavalry of the chiefs of [Ye]lumāvu. The record further states that Āḷiya-Mācheya-Daṇṇāyaka, the prime-minister of the king, who was ruling at Penu-guṇḍe granted wet and garden lands beneath the Sirivara tank to those who were appointed to worship the hero-stone.

King

Date
Śaka 1453, Khara, Śrāvaṇa, Goku-lāshṭamī.
Language
Kanarese
Remarks
Gives like the copper-plates a long eulogy in Sanskṛit and registers the grant of Chalivindla with its adjoining mountain and a number of other villages to the Śiva temple at Lēpākshi made at the instance of Virupaṇṇa. See below Part II, paragraph 74. A marginal note is added to the inscription at its right top corner which calls Virupaṇṇa, the taḷavāra of the town of Vijayanagara.

Remarks
Records the Tamil verses, composed by various authors whose names are given, eulogising certain Kāḍava chiefs. These were engraved on the Gaṇḍarādittaṉ-gōpura (tiruvāśal) under orders of Araśanārāyaṇaṉ Ālappirandāṉ Vīra-śēkhara alias Kāḍavarāyaṇ. One of the verses records that in Śaka 1108 (= 1186 A.D.) Āḷappirandāṉ Vīra-śēkharaṉ alias Kāḍavarāyaṉ son of Araśanārāyaṇaṉ Kachchiyarāyaṉ alias Kāḍavarāyaṉ destroyed Kūḍal belonging to Kaṟkaḍaga-Mārāyaṉ and also the country of Adiyamāṉ.

Language
Tamil
Remarks
Unfinished and damaged. Seems to record a compact agreed upon by the Valaṅgai and Iḍaṅgai castes that they would inflict corporal punishment on those who helped the tax collectors of the king and the Brahman landholders in the collection of taxes by coercive measures and who consented to write the accounts.
ARIE/1917-1918/C/1918/93 (page 98)
Placement
On the south wall of the maṇḍapa in front of the central shrine in the Svarṇapurīśvara temple at Kugaiyur (Kallakurichchi taluk, South Arcot district).
Dynasty
Chōḷa
King
Parakēsarivarman alias Tribhuvana-chakravartin Kulōttuṅga-Chōḷadēva, ‘who was pleased to take Madurai (Madura) and the crowned head of the Pāṇḍya.’
Date
6th year, Makara, śu. di. daśamī, Hasta.
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Registers that Kūguḍaiyāṉ Iraṇaṉ Poṉparappināṉ alias Rājarāja Kōvalarāyaṉ set up the image of Poṉparappiṉa-Īśvaramuḍaiya-Nāyaṉār, constructed the stone temple, the Śrī-Kailāsa of the village Kūgaiyūr, the arddha-maṇḍapa, the snapana-maṇḍapa, the nṛitta-maṇḍapa, the first prākāra and the gōpura, the second prākāra and the gōpura and made a gift of land for offerings and to the Brāhmaṇas of the temple. Kūgaiyūr was situated in Naṟaiyūr-kūṟ-ṟam, a subdivision of Malāḍu alias Jananātha-vaḷanāḍu.

ARIE/1917-1918/C/1918/97 (page 98)
Placement
Do.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
Śaka 1369, Prabha-va, Siṁha, ba. di. chaturthī, Mon-day, Aśvati.
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Registers an order of Vāsudēva-Nāyakar Tirumalai-Nāyakar to the people of Magadai-maṇḍalam fixing the length of the rod for measuring the wet and dry lands for the purposes of assessment. The length of the rod then in use seems to have been very small and the people threatened to migrate elsewhere. The newly prescribed rod is represented on the wall below the inscription.

Records that the second gōpura (tirumāḷigai) of the Piramīś-vara temple was built by Ammaiappaṉ Gaṇḍarasūryaṉ alias Śambuvarāyaṉ.
ARIE/1917-1918/C/1918/184 (page 106)
Placement
On the east wall of the Pātāḷīśvara temple in the same village.
Dynasty
Vijaya-nagara.
King
Kampaṇa-Uḍaiyar, son of Vīra-Bukkaṇa-Uḍaiyar.
Date
Śaka 1286, Krōdhi, Mēsha, śu. di. tṛitīyā, Wednes-day, Pūrāḍam.
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Remission of taxes, by Goppaṇaṅgaḷ, on the lands in Kulōt-tuṅga-śōḻanallūr alias Brahmīśvaram, which was an unit village in Koliyapura-paṟṟu in Paṉaiyūr-nāḍu, a subdivi-sion of Rājarāja-vaḷanāḍu belonging to the temples of Piramīśvaramuḍaiya-Nāyaṉār and Tiruppātāḷēśvaramu-ḍaiya-Nāyaṉār at Rājarāja-chaturvēdimaṅgalam which was a brahmadēya and a unit in itself.
ARIE/1917-1918/C/1918/185 (page 106)
Placement
On the south wall of the same temple.
Dynasty
Chōḷa
King
Rājakēsarivarman alias Tribhuvanachak-ravartin Kulōttuṅga-Chōḷadēva.
Date
[1]3th year
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Incomplete. Begins with the word pUmEvuvaLara, Records a gift of 16 cows for a lamp by a certain Aḻagaṉ for having missed his aim and killed another individual in a hunting excursion.
ARIE/1917-1918/C/1918/186 (page 106)
Placement
Do. do.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Tribhuvanachakravartin Kulōttuṅga-Chōḷadēva, ‘who was pleased to take Madurai (Madura), Īḻam (Ceylon) and, the crowned head of the Pāṇḍya.’
Date
26th year
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Gift of a gold diadem to Pātāḷiśvaramuḍaiya-Nāyaṉār at Rājarāja-chaturvēdimaṅgalam a brahmadēya and a village unit in Paṉaiyūr-nāḍu, a subdivision of Rājarāja-vaḷanāḍu by a merchant of Ulōgamādēvipuram a city (nagaram) in Oymā-nāḍu.
ARIE/1917-1918/C/1918/187 (page 106)
Placement
Do. do.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Parakēsarivarman alias Tribhuvanachak-ravartin Vikrama-Chōḷadēva.
Date
14th year
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Built in at the bottom. The introduction begins with the words pUmAlaimiTaintu etc. Seems to record a gift of land.
ARIE/1917-1918/C/1918/188 (page 107)
Placement
On the same wall
Dynasty
Chōḷa
King
Parakēsarivarman alias Tribhuvanachak-ravartin Uḍaiyār Rājēndra-Chōḷadēva I.
Date
24th year and 230 days, Mēsha, śu. di. Thursday, Pūram.
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Gift of land for worship and offerings in the temple of Pātāḷīśvaramuḍaiyār by Parāntakaṉ Śuttamaliyār alias Mukkōkkiḻānaḍigaḷ for the growth of the arms (bhujam vardhikka) of king Rājēndra-Chōḷa. The king was then residing in the temple of Rājarājīśvaramuḍaiyār.
ARIE/1917-1918/C/1918/189 (page 107)
Placement
Do.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Tribhuvanachakravartin Kulōttuṅga-Chōḷadēva, ‘who was pleased to take Madurai (Madura) and the crowned head of the Pāṇḍya.’
Date
16th year
Language
Tamil
Remarks
End lost and incomplete. Gift of two she-buffaloes, one ox and two calves for a lamp in the temple of Pātāḷīśvaramu-daiya-Nāyaṉār by Śeṅgēni[ma]ṅgala[miṭṭāṉ] Ammaiap-paṉ Miṭṭāṉ Appaṉ alias Chōḷēndraśiṅga Śambuvarāyaṉ.
ARIE/1917-1918/C/1918/190 (page 107)
Placement
On the steps leading to the southern entrance of the same temple.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Tribhuvanachakravartin Kulōttuṅga-Chōḷadēva.
Date
7th year
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Registers that a certain shepherd (maṉṟāḍi) residing in Eydāri, the southern hamlet of Rājarāja-chaturvēdimaṅ-galam of Paṉaiyur-nāḍu in Rājarāja-vaḷanāḍu received 32 cows and agreed to burn a perpetual lamp in the temple of Tiruppātāḷīśvaram-Uḍaiyār.

ARIE/1917-1918/C/1918/192 (page 107)
Placement
Do. do.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Parakēsarivarman alias Tribhuvanachak-ravartin Rājarājadēva.
Date
14th year, Makara, śu. di. tṛitīyā, Wednesday, Pūr-aṭṭādi.
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Begins with the introduction pUmaruviyatirumAtum, etc. Quotes the 21st year of Kulōttuṅga-Chōḷadēva. Records the gift of land by the assembly for worship to the image of Āḷuḍai-Nāchchiyār set up by Iruṅgōḷar on the day of the consecration and celebration of the marriage festival.
